Store small images in CSS

Store small pictures that cannot be shoved into sprites in data: image base64 in CSS - this saves a lot of requests to the web server.

We encode the image in base64 using online services like DailyCoding service (very convenient, nothing superfluous).
Put the resulting string in the CSS file, replacing the "TYPE" with the MIME type of your image - jpeg / png / gif or (OMG!) Bmp and "CODE" with the desired string in base64: 

.some_background { background-image: url("data:image/;base64,"); }

Now you can safely connect the necessary element to some_background style and enjoy two requests to the web server (html + css), instead of three (html + css + image).

Implementation example with images :
images.html - 361 bytes
images / images.css - 305 bytes
images / test1.png - 1 600 bytes
images / test2.png - 1,143 bytes
Total - 3 409 bytes


Base64 implementation example.
base64.html - 361 bytes
images / base64.css - 3,991 bytes
Total - 4 352 bytes


An example of the work of the finished tool Jammit :
(Google Chrome, ~ 60 Mbps):

To (102 requests, 73,23 KB transferred, 3.41 seconds):


After (2 requests, 153.88 KB transferred, 0.94 seconds):


Pros:
  • reducing the number of requests to the web server;
  • less clogging user cache;
  • sometimes reducing the effective size of the image on large files.

Minuses:
  • the complexity of updating images;
  • sometimes a slight increase in the effective volume of the image on small files.

Incomprehensibilities (incomprehensible, plus it or minus):
  • Internet Explorer 5, 6, and 7 were not added to base64 as a friend, but it works fine in IE8. You can enable it , but I do not recommend it, it is better to use mhtml (thanks to vitosik )

It seems to me that increasing the size of a CSS file is better than an extra request to a web server, since by default browsers open an average of 8 parallel connections to a web server, and 50-70 images are already a queue, and who loves queues? :)

It is worth using this method after the design and layout is approved, since it is somewhat longer to update images with this method than usual.

For automatic packaging of images in base64 there is an online service duris.ru , but you can also use a PHP script with a regular schedule : (thanks Serator ) 
 <?php echo preg_replace('/images\/[-\w\/\.]*/ie','"data:image/".((substr("\\0",-4)==".png")?"png":"gif").";base64,".base64_encode(file_get_contents("\\0"))',file_get_contents('style.css')); ?>
